## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state (x, v) and possibly time t, which is the standard first-order state-space form of mechanical oscillators. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly combine restoring forces depending on x, damping depending on v, and optional external forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped, unforced) oscillator in state form: dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper)
- Time-varying stiffness (parametric excitation): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type oscillator)
- Constant external drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (bias/constant force field)
- Harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring)
- Quadratic stiffness asymmetry: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (piecewise-like nonlinear restoring)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Quadratic drag (speed-squared): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent pumping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (another self-excited form)
- Pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; x interpreted as angle)
- Softening spring saturation: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) / (1 + c1 * x**2) - c2 * v (bounded effective stiffness at large |x|)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos-capable regime)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd restoring terms (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3) imply symmetric potentials and center the equilibrium at x = 0; adding even/asymmetric terms (e.g., -c*x*Abs(x)) shifts waveform symmetry.
- Cubic stiffness (-c*x**3) produces amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening/softening), often observable as frequency shift with larger |x|.
- Damping linear in v gives exponential energy decay near equilibrium; nonlinear damping (v**3 or v*Abs(v)) makes dissipation strongly amplitude-dependent (stronger decay at large speeds).
- Self-excitation terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v (Van der Pol) create negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|, yielding stable limit cycles.
- Pure time forcing terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) inject energy periodically and can yield resonance when forcing frequency matches the oscillator’s effective natural frequency.
- Parametric modulation (k(t)*x) with k(t)=c0+c1*cos(c*t) can destabilize the trivial solution and produce parametric resonance bands (Mathieu-type behavior).
- Using sin(c*x) instead of x indicates geometric/constraint nonlinearity (e.g., pendulum), which naturally bounds acceleration for large |x| compared with polynomial springs.
- Rational stiffness forms like x/(1+c*x**2) represent saturating restoring forces, preventing unbounded acceleration growth at large displacement.
- Presence/absence of explicit t separates autonomous oscillators (no t) from non-autonomous driven/parametric systems (t enters via forcing/modulation).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO32)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
-2.9429090494833\,x^3\;-\;0.0907042821530562\,v^3\;-\;0.594472842575296\,v\,e^{-|v|}\;+\;0.56911073046847\,\sin(t)
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly these four components and **no extra nonzero terms**:
1) \(x^3\) term only (no other \(x\)-dependence), coefficient \(-2.9429...\)  
2) \(v^3\) term, coefficient \(-0.090704...\)  
3) \(v e^{-|v|}\) term (note the exponent is \(-|v|\), not \(+|v|\)), coefficient \(-0.59447...\)  
4) pure sinusoid in \(t\) only, amplitude \(0.56911...\), frequency 1, phase 0 (but cosine with phase shift is OK)

Also, because \(v\) can be negative, terms like \(v|v|\) are **not** equivalent to \(v^3\) or \(v\), and \(e^{+|v|}\) cannot equal \(e^{-|v|}\) for all \(v\) unless the coefficient is zero.

---

### Candidate-by-candidate

1. \(c0 x^3 + c1 v^3 + c2 v e^{c3|v|} + c4\cos(c5 t+c6)+ c7 v\sin(...)\)  
   - Can match \(x^3\) via \(c0\).  
   - Can match \(v^3\) via \(c1\).  
   - Can match \(v e^{-|v|}\) by setting \(c3=-1\), \(c2=-0.59447...\).  
   - Can match \(\sin(t)\) using cosine phase shift: set \(c5=1\), \(c6=-\pi/2\), \(c4=0.56911...\) since \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\).  
   - Extra term \(c7 v\sin(...)\) must be removed: set \(c7=0\).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

2. Same as (1) but extra term \(c7 v\cos(...)\,|v|\).  
   - Set \(c7=0\) to remove it; rest as in (1).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

3. \(c0 x^3 + c1\sin(c2+c3 t)+ c4 v^3 + c5 v e^{c6|v|}+ c7\cos(c8 t+c9)\)  
   - Has *two* independent pure-time trig terms (a sine and a cosine). GT has only one. You can set one amplitude to 0.  
   - Choose \(c7=0\). Then set \(c3=1\), \(c2=0\), \(c1=0.56911...\) to get \(\sin t\).  
   - Set \(c6=-1\), \(c5=-0.59447...\).  
   - Set \(c0=-2.9429...\), \(c4=-0.090704...\).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

4. Like (1) but extra \(c7 x\sin(...)\). Set \(c7=0\). Remaining can match as in (1).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

5. Like (1) but extra \(c7 x e^{c8 v}\cos(c9 t)\). Set \(c7=0\). Remaining can match as in (1).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

6. \(c0 x^3 + c1 v^3 + c2 v^3 + c3 v e^{c4|v|} + c5\cos(...)+ c8 + c9 v|v|\)  
   - Constant term \(c8\) must be 0.  
   - \(v|v|\) term must be 0: set \(c9=0\).  
   - Combine \(v^3\) coefficients via \(c1+c2\) to equal \(-0.090704...\).  
   - Set \(c4=-1\), \(c3=-0.59447...\).  
   - Cosine can phase-shift to \(\sin t\) with \(c6=1\), \(c7=-\pi/2\), \(c5=0.56911...\).  
   - \(x^3\) via \(c0\).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

7. Like (6) but only one \(v^3\) coefficient and has constant \(c7\) and \(v|v|\). Set \(c7=0\), \(c8=0\). Then match remaining as in (1).  
   ⇒ **Matches**.

   ⇒ **Matches**.

   ⇒ **Matches**.

   - The last term depends on both \(v\) and \(t\) multiplicatively; GT has no such mixed term. Only way is set \(c7=0\).

   ⇒ **Matches**.

   ⇒ **Matches**.

   ⇒ **Matches**.
